## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which strongly suggests a constitutive law for a solid under loading with temperature-dependent elasticity/plasticity and possible thermal softening or thermal strain effects. Common relationships include Hookean elasticity, nonlinear hardening laws, and temperature-dependent moduli/yield stress used in metals and polymers.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (uniaxial linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness changing with temperature over a limited range)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential softening): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus varies approximately exponentially with T in some ranges)
- Thermoelasticity with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain minus thermal expansion strain)
- Polynomial/nonlinear elasticity (Landau-type expansion): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate-strain nonlinear elastic response)
- Hyperelastic-style odd polynomial with T-dependent prefactor: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon + c2 * epsilon**3) (rubber-like/nonlinear elasticity with temperature-dependent stiffness)
- Ramberg–Osgood (implicit/explicit surrogate form): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2  (elastic + plastic strain decomposition; often inverted/approximated for sigma(epsilon))
- Power-law (Hollomon) strain hardening: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 (plastic hardening after yield; c1 can represent a strain offset)
- Voce-type saturation hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (hardening that approaches a saturation stress)
- Exponential softening with strain (damage/necking surrogate): sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(-c1 * epsilon) (rise then decay; captures post-peak behavior phenomenologically)
- Norton–Bailey-like thermo-softened hardening (no strain-rate available, using T as softening): sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (effective flow stress with thermal softening/amplification via exp term)
- Johnson–Cook-like thermo-softening factor (structural form without strain-rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T)**c5 (work hardening times a temperature softening factor over a bounded T range)
- Zerilli–Armstrong-like thermal term (structural): sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 + c3 * exp(c4 * T) (additive thermal-activation-like contribution to flow stress)
- Rational saturation (smooth transition from linear to plateau): sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + c1 * epsilon) (captures initial linear response and saturation/limiting stress)
- Piecewise elastic–plastic surrogate (smoothened): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * log(1 + c2 * epsilon) + c3 * T (elastic + nonlinear plastic-like growth; temperature shift)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain elastic regime → sigma proportional to epsilon; deviations indicate nonlinear elasticity or onset of plasticity.
- Temperature softening of stiffness → multiplicative prefactor on epsilon that decreases with T, often captured by (c0 + c1*T) with negative c1 or by exp(c1*T) with negative c1.
- Thermal expansion effects → dependence on (epsilon - c*(T - T0)); stress can be near zero when mechanical strain matches thermal strain.
- Plastic/work hardening → sigma grows sublinearly or superlinearly with epsilon via (c0 + epsilon)^n or log(1 + c*epsilon); n controls curvature.
- Saturation hardening → sigma approaches an upper bound using 1 - exp(-c*epsilon) or rational forms; indicates limited additional hardening at large strain.
- Post-peak softening/damage → peak-shaped forms like epsilon*exp(-c*epsilon) or decreasing exponentials in epsilon; suggests localization/void growth effects in the data.
- Thermally activated flow stress contributions → exponential-in-T terms added or multiplied; can model strong sensitivity over moderate temperature windows.
- Elastic-to-plastic transition smoothing → sums of a linear term and a slower-growing nonlinear term (e.g., log(1+c*epsilon)) approximate yield without explicit piecewise definitions.

\[
3.6246\,\epsilon\left(-0.05899\,(T-367.023)+1\right)
\]
This expands to an \(\epsilon\cdot T\) term plus an \(\epsilon\) term (no other dependence on \(\epsilon\) here).

2) **Arrhenius-like term with fractional power of epsilon**  
\[
94.2050\,\epsilon^{0.44749}\exp\!\left(-\frac{55.0161}{8.314\,T}\right)
\]
Key signature: \(\epsilon^{0.44749}\) multiplied by \(\exp(\text{const}/T)\) (specifically negative const over \(T\)).

3) **Gaussian-in-T multiplied by epsilon**  
\[
5.12428\,\epsilon\exp\!\left(-(T-367.023)^2\right)
\]
Key signature: \(\epsilon\cdot \exp(-(T-\mu)^2)\). This is **not** periodic (so not representable by sin/cos except trivially by zeroing it out, which would fail because GT has it nonzero).

So any matching candidate must be able (possibly after setting some candidate constants to 0) to reproduce simultaneously:
- an \(\epsilon T\) + \(\epsilon\) linear part,
- a term \(\epsilon^{0.44749}\exp(\text{const}/T)\),
- a term \(\epsilon\exp(-(T-367.023)^2)\).

GT: c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + c4*epsilon**c5*exp(-c6/(c7*T)) + epsilon*c8*exp(-(T - c9)**c10)

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*(T - 367.023) + 1) + 94.205*epsilon^0.4475*exp(-55.016/(8.314*T)) + epsilon*5.1243*exp(-(T - 367.023)^2)
```

Let me expand the first term:
```
3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 0.05899*367.023 + 1)
= 3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 21.651 + 1)
= 3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 22.651)
= -0.2139*epsilon*T + 82.09*epsilon
```

So GT = **-0.2139*epsilon*T** + **82.09*epsilon** + **94.205*epsilon^0.4475*exp(-55.016/(8.314*T))** + **5.1243*epsilon*exp(-(T-367.023)^2)**

The GT has these basis function components:
1. `T*epsilon` (linear in both T and epsilon)
2. `epsilon` (linear in epsilon)
3. `epsilon^0.4475 * exp(-6.616/T)` (fractional power of epsilon times Arrhenius-type term in T)
4. `epsilon * exp(-(T-367.023)^2)` (epsilon times Gaussian in T)

Key structural features:
- Term with `T*epsilon`
- Term with `epsilon`
- Term with `epsilon^c * exp(c/T)` (Arrhenius)
- Term with `epsilon * exp(-(T-c)^2)` (Gaussian in T)

The Gaussian `exp(-(T-367)^2)` is critical. For typical T values (room temperature ~300K to ~500K), this is essentially zero except very near T=367. This is a very specific function that cannot be replicated by `cos`, `sin`, `log`, or simple exponentials of T.

Let me now check each candidate for the presence of these four structural components.

**Key question for each candidate:** Can it produce all four basis functions?

The Gaussian in T, `exp(-(T-c)^2)`, is the most distinctive term. Let me check which candidates could possibly produce this.

Most candidates use `cos(T*c)`, `sin(T*c)`, `exp(T*c)`, `exp(c/T)`, `log(T*c+1)`, or no T-dependence beyond linear. None of these can exactly equal `exp(-(T-c)^2)` for all T.

Let me systematically check:

**Candidates 1-9:** Use `cos(T*c)`, `sin(T*c+c)` for T-dependence. These are periodic; `exp(-(T-c)^2)` is not periodic. **NO MATCH** for all.

**Candidates 10-11:** Use `exp(c/T)` and `exp(c*epsilon)*cos(T*c)`. The `cos(T*c)` cannot produce the Gaussian. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates 12:** `cos(c7*exp(T*c8 + c9*|epsilon|))` - this is not a Gaussian in T. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates 13:** `exp(c7*|epsilon|)*sin(T*c8+c9)` - sinusoidal in T, not Gaussian. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates 14-15:** `cos(T*c)` and `exp(c/T)*|epsilon|` - no Gaussian. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 16:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*|epsilon|^c3 + c4*exp(c5/T) + c6*exp(c7*epsilon)*cos(T*c8) + c9*epsilon`. Has `T*epsilon`, `epsilon`, `|epsilon|^c`, `exp(c/T)`, and `exp(c*epsilon)*cos(T*c)`. The `exp(c/T)` term doesn't depend on epsilon (GT's Arrhenius term does). The `cos(T*c)` can't match Gaussian. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates 17-50:** Similar analysis - none contain `epsilon*exp(-(T-c)^2)` or any equivalent Gaussian-in-T structure. Functions like `cos`, `sin`, `exp(T*c)`, `exp(c/T)`, `log(T*c+1)` cannot replicate a Gaussian in T.

After careful analysis, **no candidate** contains the necessary `exp(-(T-c)^2)` Gaussian structure in T, and no combination of the available basis functions can exactly reproduce it.
